## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically affects elastic modulus and flow stress through thermal softening or thermally activated mechanisms, while strain governs the mechanical response through elastic or plastic deformation laws.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon (Hooke's law at constant T)
- Temperature-dependent elasticity: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear thermal softening of modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (exponential thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain curve)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic combined)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1/T)) (thermally activated flow stress)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elasticity)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 * T)**c2 (power-law temperature dependence)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Coupled power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * T * sinh(c1 * epsilon) (hyperbolic sine constitutive model)
- Johnson-Cook full thermal: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (JC with exponential thermal term)
- Ludwik model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal effect)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear stress-strain at small strains transitioning to nonlinear at large strains → piecewise or power-law hardening epsilon**c with c<1
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → multiplicative factor that decreases with T, such as (T_m - T) or exp(-c*T)
- Stress saturation at large strains → saturating functions like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon)
- Thermally activated deformation processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) multiplicative factors
- Separation of strain hardening and thermal softening → product form f(epsilon) * g(T) indicating independent mechanisms
- Strain rate sensitivity analog through temperature → sinh or exponential functions of strain scaled by temperature
- Phase transformation or melting effects → sharp transitions near critical temperatures modeled by sigmoidal T-dependence
- Negative temperature coefficient of strength → monotonically decreasing function of T multiplying the strain term

The inverse-5th-power rational term provides a localized T-scaled contribution near ε≈0 (c3≈1.04). The ε-only polynomial has parameters at boundary values (c6=c8=100, c7≈-100), forming 100(ε²-ε+1), which suggests possible parameter saturation and that this large T-independent offset may be compensating for structural limitations. GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci4)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*log(epsilon + c4)
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `90.776*epsilon**2 + 2.482*(T - 337.769)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Expanding: `90.776*epsilon**2 + 2.482*T*log(epsilon + 1) - 838.627*log(epsilon + 1)`

So the GT has three structural components:
1. `epsilon**2` term (coefficient ≈ 90.776)
2. `T*log(epsilon + 1)` term (coefficient ≈ 2.482)
3. `log(epsilon + 1)` term (coefficient ≈ -838.627)

I need candidates that can produce: `a*epsilon**2 + b*T*log(epsilon+1) + c*log(epsilon+1)`

**Key observation:** `log(epsilon + 1)` can come from `exp(c*epsilon)` only if c=0, giving exp(0)=1 (constant), so that won't help. I need explicit `log` terms.

Let me check candidates with `log` terms:

**Candidate 21:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*log(T*c6 + 1) + c7/(c8*epsilon + c9)`

This has `log(c4*epsilon+1)` but not `T*log(epsilon+1)`. The `log(T*c6+1)` doesn't give `T*log(...)`. Can't match.

**Candidate 44:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + T**c3*c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon + c8) + c9`

Setting c2=0: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T**c3*c4*log(c5*epsilon+1) + c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9`

Set c3=1: gives `T*c4*log(c5*epsilon+1)` — this gives the `T*log(epsilon+1)` term with c5=1.

Now I need `log(epsilon+1)` (without T) and `epsilon**2`. 

Setting c0=0 removes `T*epsilon`. Then `T*c1` is a pure T term — unwanted unless c1=0.

With c1=0, c0=0: `T*c4*log(c5*epsilon+1) + c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9`

I need `epsilon**2` and `log(epsilon+1)` from `c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9`. But `epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8)` is a rational function, not `epsilon**2` or `log`. Can't match.

**Candidate 46:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3/(c4*epsilon + c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*epsilon) + 1)`

Note: `log(c7*exp(c8*epsilon)+1)`. If c8=0: `log(c7+1)` = constant. Not helpful.

If c7 is very large: `log(c7) + c8*epsilon` approximately. Not helpful for `log(epsilon+1)`.

**Candidate 24:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3*exp(c4*epsilon)*log(T*c5 + 1)`

Set c2=0: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c3*exp(c4*epsilon)*log(T*c5+1)`. This gives `exp(c4*epsilon)*log(T*c5+1)` — not `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

**Candidate 48:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + T*c3*epsilon**2 + c4*epsilon/(c5*epsilon+c6) + c7/(c5*epsilon+c6)`

Set c2=0: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c3*epsilon**2 + (c4*epsilon+c7)/(c5*epsilon+c6)`

This gives `T*c3*epsilon**2` but I need `epsilon**2` without T, and `T*log(epsilon+1)` which isn't available here.

After extensive checking, none of the candidates contain the structural form `T*log(epsilon + constant)` combined with `epsilon**2` and `log(epsilon + constant)` that would be needed to match the GT.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci4)

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*log(epsilon + c4)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 90.776*epsilon² + 2.482*(T - 337.769)*log(epsilon + 1)**

Expanding: **90.776*epsilon² + 2.482*T*log(epsilon+1) - 838.769*log(epsilon+1)**

Key basis functions in GT:
- epsilon² (pure, no T dependence)
- T*log(epsilon+1)
- log(epsilon+1) (pure, no T dependence)

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

For many candidates, the structure is `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + ...`. Note that `T*log(epsilon+1)` from GT is NOT `T*epsilon` (they're different basis functions). However, if we can set c0=0 to eliminate T*epsilon, and if `T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon)` with c2=0 gives `T*c1` which is just linear in T (not T*log(epsilon+1)), that won't work either.

The GT requires `T*log(epsilon+1)` as a basis function. Let me check which candidates can produce this.

**Key observation:** Most candidates have terms like `T*c0*epsilon`, `T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon)`, `T*c3/(c4+epsilon)^5`, etc. None of these produce `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

Some candidates have `log(T*c5+1)` terms or `exp(c*epsilon)*log(T*c+1)` terms - these have log in T, not log in epsilon multiplied by T.

Let me look for candidates that can produce `T*log(epsilon+1)`:

- **Candidate 44**: Has `T^c3 * c4 * log(c5*epsilon+1)`. If c3=1, this gives `T*c4*log(c5*epsilon+1)` — this IS `T*log(epsilon+1)` with c5=1! Then we need epsilon² and log(epsilon+1). The remaining terms: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9`. Set c0=0, c1=0 (or c2=0 and absorb). With c1=0: remaining is `c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9`. This is a rational function in epsilon — it cannot produce epsilon² or log(epsilon+1). **NO MATCH.**

- **Candidate 29**: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3*epsilon/(c4*epsilon+c5) + c6 + c7*epsilon^c8*exp(c9/T)`. The term `c7*epsilon^c8*exp(c9/T)` mixes T and epsilon in a way that can't give T*log(epsilon+1). **NO MATCH.**

Let me check ALL candidates for the ability to produce `T*log(epsilon+1)`:

Going through systematically, I find that **none** of the candidates contain a term that can produce `T*log(epsilon+1)`. The log terms present are either `log(T*c+1)` (log of T, not epsilon), or `log(c*epsilon+1)` without T multiplication (except Candidate 44 with `T^c3`), or `exp()*log()` combinations.

**Candidate 44** is the closest: `T^c3 * c4 * log(c5*epsilon+1)` with c3=1 gives T*log(epsilon+1). But then we need `90.776*epsilon² - 838.769*log(epsilon+1)`. The remaining terms `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9` — setting c0=0, c2=0 gives `T*c1 + c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9`. The T*c1 term is unwanted (can't be zeroed without losing needed terms), and we can't get epsilon² from a rational function. Set c1=0: then `c6*epsilon/(c7*epsilon+c8) + c9` cannot produce epsilon² - log(epsilon+1). **NO MATCH.**

After careful analysis, none of the 50 candidates can produce the required `T*log(epsilon+1)` basis function combined with epsilon² and log(epsilon+1).
